• Anderson, R. M., and May, R. M. [3mInfectious Diseases of Humans [0m(Oxford University Press, Oxford, 1991). 

• Murray, J. D. [3mMathematical Biology, [0m2d ed. (Springer, Heidelberg, 1993). 

A small but excellent collection of papers dealing with the spread of infectious diseases on networks is: 

•• Ball, F., Mollison, D., and Scalia-Tomba, G. Epidemics with two levels of mixing. [3mAnnals of Applied Probability, [0m7(1), 46–89 
(1997). 

⋆⋆ Hess, G. Disease in metapopulation models: Implications for conservation. [3mEcology, [0m77, 1617–1632 (1996). 

⋆⋆ Kareiva, P. Population dynamics in spatially complex environments: Theory and data. [3mPhilosophical Transactions of the Royal 
Society of London, Series B, [0m330, 175–190 (1988). 

• Kretschmar, M., and Morris, M. Measures of concurrency in networks and the spread of infectious disease. [3mMathematical 
Biosciences, [0m133, 165–195 (1996). 

⋆⋆ Longini, I. M., Jr. A mathematical model for predicting the geographic spread of new infectious agents. [3mMathematical 
Biosciences, [0m90, 367–383 (1988). 

• Sattenspiel, L., and Simon, C. P. The spread and persistence of infectious diseases in structured populations. [3mMathematical 
Biosciences, [0m90, 341–366 (1988). 

[1m(٤) الأوبئة في عالم صغير [0m

The most complete account of the early work on disease spreading on small-world networks is chapter 6 of: 

⋆⋆ Watts, D. J. [3mSmall Worlds: The Dynamics of Networks between Order and Randomness [0m(Princeton University Press, Princeton, NJ, 
1999). 

A number of subsequent results about epidemics on networks have been published in the following papers: 

• Boots, M., and A. Sasaki. “Small worlds” and the evolution of virulence: Infection occurs locally and at a distance. [3mProceedings 
of the Royal Society of London, Series B, [0m266, 1933–1938 (1999). 

• Keeling, M. J. The effects of local spatial structure on epidemiological invasions. [3mProceedings of the Royal Society of London, 
Series B, [0m266, 859–867 (1999). 

• Kuperman, M., and Abramson, G. Small world effect in an epidemiological model. [3mPhysical Review Letters, [0m86, 2909–2912 (2001). 

Some excellent works on the foot-and-mouth epidemic, and a fine example of mathematical modeling contributing to policy decisions, 
are: 

⋆⋆ Ferguson, N. M., Donnelly, C. A., and Anderson, R. M. The foot-and-mouth epidemic in Great Britain: Pattern of spread and 
impact of interventions. [3mScience, [0m292, 1155–1160 (2001). 

⋆⋆ Ferguson, N. M., Donnelly, C. A., and Anderson, R. M. Transmission intensity and impact of control policies on the foot and 
mouth epidemic in Great Britain. [3mNature, [0m413, 542–548 (2001). 

⋆⋆ Keeling, M. J., Woolhouse, M. E. J., Shaw, D. J., Matthews, L., Chase-Topping, M., Haydon, D. T., Cornell, S. J., Kappey, J., 
Wilesmith, J., and Grenfell, B. T. Dynamics of the 2001 UK foot and mouth epidemic: Stochastic dispersal in a heterogeneous 
landscape. [3mScience, [0m294, 813–817 (2001). 

The discovery that diseases spreading in scale-free networks don’t exhibit an epidemic threshold is reported in: 

• Pastor-Satorras, R., and Vespignani, A. Epidemic spreading in scale-free networks. [3mPhysical Review Letters, [0m86, 3200–3203 
(2001). 

Pastor-Satorras and Vespignani have continued to work on disease spreading in scale-free networks. Their findings are summarized 
in: 

• Pastor-Satorras, R., and Vespignani, A. Epidemics and immunization in scale-free networks. In Bornholdt, S., and Schuster, H. G. 
(eds.), [3mHandbook of Graphs and Networks: From the Genome to the Internet [0m(Wiley-VCH, Berlin, 2002). 

Some empirical support for their assumption of a scale-free e-mail network is reported in: 

• Ebel, H., Mielsch, L. I., and Bornholdt, S. Scale-free topology of e-mail networks. [3mPhysical Review E, [0m66, 035103 (2002). 

The public health impact of needle exchange programs is analyzed in a report for the [3mJournal of the American Medical Association [0m
by the Center for AIDS Prevention Studies, University of California, San Francisco, found at 
http://www.ama-assn.org/special/hiv/preventn/prevent3.htm. 

An earlier report prepared for the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention can be found at 
http://www.caps.ucsf.edu/capsweb/publications/ needlereport.html. 

[1m(٥) نماذج التخلل للأمراض [0m

The best introduction to the subject of percolation is the following (which even manages to be funny in places): 

• Stauffer, D., and Aharony, A. [3mIntroduction to Percolation Theory [0m(Taylor and Francis, London, 1992). 

The details of my work with Mark Newman on a site percolation approach to disease spreading on small-world network are given in: 

• Newman, M. E. J., and Watts, D. J. Scaling and percolation in the small-world network model. [3mPhysical Review E, [0m60, 7332–7342 
(1999). 

[1m(٦) الشبكات والفيروسات ومايكروسوفت [0m

Mark Newman and Cris Moore’s work on site and bond percolation is described in the following: 

• Moore, C., and Newman, M. E. J. Epidemics and percolation in small-world networks. [3mPhysical Review E, [0m61, 5678–5682 (2000). 

•• Moore, C., and Newman, M. E. J. Exact solution of site and bond percolation on small-world networks. [3mPhysical Review E, [0m62, 
7059–7064 (2000). 

[1m(٧) الأعطال والقوة [0m

The original paper using percolation ideas to quantify network robustness is: 

⋆⋆ Albert, R., Jeong, H., and Barabási, A. L. Attack and error tolerance of complex networks. [3mNature, [0m406, 378–382 (2000). 

Soon after, a series of papers examined the topic in greater detail. They are: 

• Callaway, D. S., Newman, M. E. J., Strogatz, S. H., and Watts, D. J. Network robustness and fragility: Percolation on random 
graphs. [3mPhysical Review Letters, [0m85, 5468–5471 (2000). 

• Cohen, R., Erez, K., ben-Avraham, D., and Havlin, S. Resilience of the Internet to random breakdowns. [3mPhysical Review Letters, [0m
85, 4626–4628 (2000). 

• Cohen, R., Erez, K., ben-Avraham, D., and Havlin, S. Breakdown of the Internet under intentional attack. [3mPhysical Review 
Letters, [0m86, 3682–3685 (2001). 

[1mالفصل السابع: القرارات والأوهام وجنون الجماهير [0m

[1m(١) اقتصاديات التيوليب [0m

Charles Mackay’s classic account of mania, financial and otherwise, has been reprinted many times. A relatively recent version is: 

⋆ Mackay, C. [3mExtraordinary Popular Delusions and the Madness of Crowds [0m(Harmony Books, New York, 1980). 

Some other recent treatises on the same subject are: 

⋆ Kindleberger, C. P. [3mManias, Panics, and Crashes: A History of Financial Crises, [0m4th ed. (Wiley, New York, 2000). 

⋆ Shiller, R. J. Irrational Exuberance (Princeton University Press, Princeton, NJ, 2000). 

[1m(٢) الخوف والطمع والعقلانية [0m

Adam Smith’s discussion of rationally optimizing agents, including his reference to the invisible hand, is in: 

⋆ Smith, A. [3mThe Wealth of Nations, [0mVol. 1, Book 4 (University of Chicago Press, Chicago, 1976), chapter 2, p. 477. 

The paradox of the efficient market hypothesis is described in: 

⋆ Chancellor, E. [3mDevil Take the Hindmost: A History of Financial Speculation [0m(Farrar, Straus and Giroux, New York, 1999). 

And some recent work on constructing a more realistic vision of both investor and financial-market behavior, in which dynamics is 
a crucial ingredient, is: 

• Farmer, J. D. Market force, ecology, and evolution. [3mIndustrial and Corporate Change, [0mforthcoming (2002). 

• Farmer, J. D., and Joshi, S. The price dynamics of common trading strategies. [3mJournal of Economic Behavior and Organization, [0m
49(2), 149–171 (2002). 

⋆⋆ Farmer, J. D., and Lo, A. Frontiers of finance: Evolution and efficient markets. [3mProceedings of the National Academy of 
Sciences, [0m96, 9991-9992 (1999). 

[1m(٣) القرارات الجمعية [0m

The technical paper by Natalie Glance and Bernardo Huberman, describing the diner’s dilemma and the conditions under which it can 
be resolved, is: 

• Glance, N. S., and Huberman, B. A. The outbreak of cooperation. [3mJournal of Mathematical Sociology, [0m17(4), 281–302 (1993). 

A more accessible description of the same results is: 

⋆ Glance, N. S., and Huberman, B. A. The dynamics of social dilemmas. [3mScientific American, [0m270(3), 76–81 (1994). 

The literature on the evolution of cooperation is gigantic and spans several disciplines—evolutionary biology, economics, 
political science, and sociology in particular. It is impossible even to provide a representative list of publications, but some 
important contributions are: 

⋆⋆ Axelrod, R. [3mThe Evolution of Cooperation [0m(Basic Books, New York, 1984). 

⋆⋆ Axelrod, R., and Dion, D. The further evolution of cooperation. [3mScience, [0m242, 1385–1390 (1988). 

• Boorman, S. A., and Levitt, P. R. [3mThe Genetics of Altruism [0m(Academic Press, New York, 1980). 

⋆⋆ Boyd, R. S., and Richerson, P. J. The evolution of reciprocity in sizable groups. [3mJournal of Theoretical Biology, [0m132, 337–356 
(1988). 

⋆⋆ Hardin, G. The tragedy of the commons. [3mScience, [0m162, 1243–1248 (1968). 

⋆⋆ Huberman, B. A., and Lukose, R. M. Social dilemmas and Internet congestion. [3mScience, [0m277, 535–537 (1997). 

⋆⋆ Nowak, M. A., and May, R. M. Evolutionary games and spatial chaos. [3mNature, [0m359, 826–829 (1992). 

⋆⋆ Olson, M. [3mThe Logic of Collective Action: Public Goods and the Theory of Groups [0m(Harvard University Press, Cambridge, MA, 
1965). 

⋆ Ostrom, E., Burger, J., Field, C. B., Norgaard, R. B., and Policansky, D. Revisiting the commons: Local lessons, global 
challenges. [3mScience, [0m284, 278–282 (1999). 

[1m(٤) سلاسل المعلومات [0m

The literature on information cascades is, again, multidisciplinary and eclectic. Some examples are: 

⋆⋆ Aguirre, B. E., Quarantelli, E. L., and Mendoza, J. L. The collective behavior of fads: The characteristics, effects, and 
career of streaking. [3mAmerican Sociological Review, [0m53, 569–584 (1988). 

• Banerjee, A. V. A simple model of herd behavior. [3mQuarterly Journal of Economics, [0m107, 797–817 (1992). 

• Bikhchandani, S., Hirshleifer, D., and Welch, I. A theory of fads, fashion, custom and cultural change as informational 
cascades. [3mJournal of Political Economy, [0m100(5), 992–1026 (1992). 

⋆⋆ Lohmann, S. The dynamics of informational cascades: The Monday demonstrations in Leipzig, East Germany, 1989–91. [3mWorld 
Politics, [0m47, 42–101 (1994). 

[1m(٥) مؤثرات المعلومات الخارجية [0m

A description of Asch’s original experiment is given in: 

⋆ Asch, S. E. Effects of group pressure upon the modification and distortion of judgments. In Cartwright, D., and Zander, A. 
(eds.), [3mGroup Dynamics: Research and Theory [0m(Row, Peterson, Evanston, IL, 1953), pp. 151–162. 

Herbert Simon’s theory of bounded rationality is espoused in: 

⋆⋆ Simon, H. A., Egidi, M., and Marris, R. L. [3mEconomics, Bounded Rationality and the Cognitive Revolution [0m(Edward Elgar, 
Brookfield, VT, 1992). 

[1m(٦) المؤثرات الخارجية القسرية [0m

The spread of crime via a network of peer pressure relationships is considered (in a theoretical manner) in: 

⋆⋆ Glaeser, E. L., Sacerdote, B., and Schheinkman, J. A. Crime and social interactions. [3mQuarterly Journal of Economics, [0m111, 
507–548 (1996). 

The paper introducing the concept of a spiral of silence in voting behavior is: 

⋆ Noelle-Neumann, E. Turbulences in the climate of opinion: Methodological applications of the spiral of silence theory. [3mPublic 
Opinion Quarterly, [0m41(2), 143–158 (1977). 

[1m(٧) مؤثرات السوق الخارجية [0m

The principal exponent of what is now called lock-in via increasing returns is the economist Brian Arthur. His groundbreaking 
paper (which took him many years to find a journal that would publish it) is: 

• Arthur, W. B. Competing technologies, increasing returns, and lock-in by historical events. [3mEconomic Journal, [0m99(394), 116–131 
(1989). 

Another, slightly different, approach to the topic of increasing returns is espoused in: 

• Romer, P. Increasing returns and long-run growth. [3mJournal of Political Economy, [0m94(5), 1002–1034 (1986). 

Although the authors do not link it to the subject of network externalities, the importance of complementarities is emphasized in: 

• Milgrom, P., and Roberts, J. The economics of modern manufacturing: Technology, strategy, and organization. [3mAmerican Economic 
Review, [0m80(3), 511–528 (1990). 

Meanwhile, the prevailing economics approach to so-called network externalities is described in: 

⋆⋆ Economides, N. The economics of networks. [3mInternational Journal of Industrial Organization, [0m16(4), 673–699 (1996). 

[1m(٨) مؤثرات التنسيق الخارجية [0m

Although neither of these papers uses the term, the relevance of externalities to decisions about cooperation is evident in: 

• Glance, N. S., and Huberman, B. A. The outbreak of cooperation. [3mJournal of Mathematical Sociology, [0m17(4), 281–302 (1993). 

⋆⋆ Kim, H., and Bearman, P. The structure and dynamics of movement participation. [3mAmerican Sociological Review, [0m62(1), 70–94 
(1997). 

[1m(٩) صناعة القرار اجتماعيًّا [0m

The report on body piercing is: 

⋆ Harden, B. Coming to grips with the enduring appeal of body piercing. [3mNew York Times, [0mFebruary 12, 2002, p. A16. 

[1mالفصل الثامن: الحدود والسلاسل وقابلية التنبؤ [0m

[1m(١) نماذج حدود القرارات [0m

The earliest use of threshold models as a way of understanding collective decision making is probably: 

⋆⋆ Schelling, T. C. A study of binary choices with externalities. [3mJournal of Conflict Resolution, [0m17(3), 381–428 (1973). 

Another early classic is: 

⋆⋆ Granovetter, M. Threshold models of collective behavior. [3mAmerican Journal of Sociology, [0m83(6), 1420–1443 (1978). 

The actual derivation of a threshold model depends on what kind of decision an individual is making, and what sort of decision 
externalities pertain. Some examples of quite different derivations, all of which effectively generate threshold rules are: 

• Arthur, W. B., and Lane, D. A. Information contagion. [3mStructural Change and Economic Dynamics, [0m4(1), 81–103 (1993). 

• Boorman, S. A., and Levitt, P. R. [3mThe Genetics of Altruism [0m(Academic Press, New York, 1980). 

• Durlauf, S. N. A framework for the study of individual behavior and social interactions. [3mSociological Methodology, [0m31, 47–87 
(2001). 

• Glance, N. S., and Huberman, B. A. The outbreak of cooperation. [3mJournal of Mathematical Sociology, [0m17(4), 281–302 (1993). 

• Morris, S. N. Contagion. [3mReview of Economic Studies, [0m67, 57–78 (2000). 

[1m(٣) السلاسل في الشبكات الاجتماعية [0m

Some information about [3mIthaca hours [0mcan be found in: 

⋆ Glover, P. Grassroots economics. [3mIn Context, [0m41, 30 (1995). 

⋆ Morse, M. Dollars or sense. [3mUtne Reader, [0m99 (September–October 1999). 

Everett Rogers’ classic reference on the diffusion of innovations, in which much of the still-current terminology was introduced, 
was first published in 1962. It is now in its fourth edition: 

⋆ Rogers, E. [3mThe Diffusion of Innovations, [0m4th ed. (Free Press, New York, 1995). 

A valiant attempt to combine Rogers’ ideas with concepts from social network analysis is by one of Rogers’ students, Thomas 
Valente: 

⋆⋆ Valente, T. W. [3mNetwork Models of the Diffusion of Innovations [0m(Hampton Press, Cresskill, NJ, 1995). 

⋆ Coleman, J. S., Katz, E., and Menzel, H. The diffusion of an innovation among physicians. [3mSociometry, [0m20(4), 253–270 (1957). 

[1m(٤) السلاسل والتخلل [0m

The paper summarizing the threshold model approach to information cascades on networks is: 

• Watts, D. J. A simple model of global cascades on random networks. [3mProceedings of the National Academy of Sciences, [0m99, 
5766–5771 (2002). 

[1m(٥) التحولات الطورية والسلاسل [0m

Malcolm Gladwell’s engaging discussion of social contagion is: 

⋆ Gladwell, M. [3mThe Tipping Point: How Little Things Can Make a Big Difference [0m(Little, Brown, New York, 2000). 

[1m(٦) تجاوز الصدع [0m

Geoffrey Moore’s descriptive account of the “chasm” between early adopters and the early to late majority is given in: 

⋆ Moore, G. A. [3mCrossing the Chasm: Marketing and Selling High-Tech Products to Mainstream Customers [0m(Harper Business, New York, 
1999). 

[1m(٧) وجهة نظر غير خطية للتاريخ [0m

The distinction between quality and success is made apparent in Art De Vany’s study of the movie industry: 

⋆⋆ De Vany, A., and Lee, C. Quality signals in information cascades and the dynamics of motion picture box office revenues: A 
computational model. [3mJournal of Economic Dynamics and Control, [0m25, 593–614 (2001). 

• De Vany, A. S., and Walls, W. D. Bose-Einstein dynamics and adaptive contracting in the motion picture industry. [3mEconomic 
Journal, [0m106, 1493–1514 (1996). 

[1m(٩) عودة إلى القوة [0m

The related notions of normal accidents and robust-yet-fragile systems are presented in two very different works: 

⋆ Perrow, C. [3mNormal Accidents: Living with High-Risk Technologies [0m(Basic Books, New York, 1984). 

• Carlson, J. M., and Doyle, J. Highly optimized tolerance: A mechanism for power laws in designed systems. [3mPhysical Review E, [0m
60(2), 1412–1427 (1999). 

[1mالفصل التاسع: الابتكار والتكيُّف والتعافي [0m

[1m(١) أزمة تويوتا-آيسين [0m

The account of the Toyota-Aisin crisis on which my description is based is: 

⋆ Nishiguchi, T., and Beaudet, A. Fractal design: Self-organizing links in supply chain management. In Von Krogh, G., Nonaka, I., 
and Nishiguchi, T. (eds.), [3mKnowledge Creation: A Source of Value [0m(Macmillan, London, 2000). 

Another paper about the remarkable Toyota group that guided our thinking on innovation is: 

⋆ Ward, A., Liker, J. K., Cristiano, J. J., and Sobek, D. K. The second Toyota paradox: How delaying decisions can make better 
cars faster. [3mSloan Management Review, [0m36(3), 43–51 (1995). 

[1m(٢) الأسواق والهياكل الهرمية [0m

The original text—and still one of the greatest—on industrial organization is: 

⋆ Smith, A. [3mThe Wealth of Nations [0m(University of Chicago Press, Chicago, 1976). 

A precursor to Coase’s theory of transaction costs was Frank Knight’s claim that firms exist to reduce uncertainty: 

⋆⋆ Knight, F. H. [3mRisk, Uncertainty, and Profit [0m(London School of Economics and Political Science, London, 1933). 

And Ronald Coase’s original argument of transaction costs as the basis for the firm is explicated in: 

⋆ Coase, R. The nature of the firm. [3mEconomica, [0mn.s., 4 (November 1937). 

Several decades later, Coase is still trying to get his ideas accepted by mainstream economics. His latest attempt is: 

⋆ Coase, R. [3mThe Nature of the Firm [0m(Oxford University Press, Oxford, 1991). 

The chief proponent of the hierarchical structure of firms is Oliver Williamson, whose views are expressed comprehensively in: 

⋆⋆ Williamson, O. [3mE. Markets and Hierarchies [0m(Free Press, New York, 1975). 

A shorter version is: 

⋆⋆ Williamson, O. E. Transaction cost economics and organization theory. In Smelser, N. J., and Swedberg, R. (eds.), [3mThe Handbook 
of Economic Sociology [0m(Princeton University Press, Princeton, NJ, 1994), pp. 77–107. 

The superiority of the hierarchy has been extensively formalized and developed in recent years by a small group of economists, led 
by Roy Radner. Some of the principal works of this literature are: 

• Bolton, P., and Dewatripont, M. The firm as a communication network. [3mQuarterly Journal of Economics, [0m109(4), 809–839 (1994). 

• Radner, R. The organization of decentralized information processing. [3mEconometrica, [0m61(5), 1109–1146 (1993). 

• Radner, R. Bounded rationality, indeterminacy, and the theory of the firm. [3mEconomic Journal, [0m106, 1360–1373 (1996). 

• Van Zandt, T. Decentralized information processing in the theory of organizations. In Sertel, M. (ed.), [3mContemporary Economic 
Issues, [0mvol. 4: [3mEconomic Design and Behavior [0mp. 125–160 (Macmillan, London, 1999), chapter 7. 

[1m(٣) التقسيمات الصناعية [0m

Michael Piore and Chuck Sabel’s groundbreaking book on the changing nature of the global economy is: 

⋆ Piore, M. J., and Sabel, C. F. [3mThe Second Industrial Divide: Possibilities for Prosperity [0m(Basic Books, New York, 1984). 

[1m(٤) الغموض [0m

The paper describing Honda’s system for identifying problems in their manufacturing plants is: 

⋆ MacDuffie, J. P. The road to “root cause”: Shop-floor problemsolving at three auto assembly plants. [3mManagement Science, [0m43, 4 
(1997). 

A variety of approaches to the theory of the internal architecture of the firm have been taken within the economics, sociology, 
and business communities. It is a vast literature. An eclectic collection of readings, with no claim to being exhaustive or even 
representative, is as follows: 

⋆ Chandler, A. D. [3mThe Visible Hand: The Managerial Revolution in American Business [0m(Belknap Press of Harvard University Press, 
Cambridge, MA, 1977). 

⋆ Clippinger, J. (ed.). [3mThe Biology of Business: Decoding the Natural Laws of the Enterprise [0m(Jossey-Bass, San Francisco, 1999). 

• Fama, E. F. Agency problems and the theory of the firm. [3mJournal of Political Economy, [0m88, 288–307 (1980). 

⋆⋆ Hart, O. [3mFirms, Contracts and Financial Structure [0m(Oxford University Press, New York, 1995). 

⋆⋆ March, J. G., and Simon, H. A. [3mOrganizations [0m(Blackwell, Oxford, 1993). 

⋆⋆ Nelson, R. R., and Winter, S. G. [3mAn Evolutionary Theory of Economic Change [0m(Belknap Press of Harvard University Press, 
Cambridge, MA, 1982). 

⋆⋆ Powell, W., and DiMaggio, P. (eds.). [3mThe New Institutionalism in Organizational Analysis [0m(Chicago, University of Chicago Press, 
1991). 

• Sah, R. K., and Stiglitz, J. E. The architecture of economic systems: Hierarchies and polyarchies. [3mAmerican Economic Review, [0m
76(4), 716–727 (1986). 

[1m(٥) الطريقة الثالثة [0m

An indication of Chuck’s understanding of the problem at the time we started working together is given in the following: 

⋆ Helper, S., MacDuffie, J. P., and Sabel, C. F. Pragmatic collaborations: Advancing knowledge while controlling opportunism. [3m
Industrial and Corporate Change, [0m9(3), 443–488 (2000). 

⋆ Sabel, C. F. Diversity, not specialization: The ties that bind the (new) industrial district. In Quadrio Curzio, A., and Fortis, 
M. (eds.), [3mComplexity and Industrial Clusters: Dynamics and Models in Theory and Practice [0m(Physica-Verlag, Heidelberg, 2002). 

[1m(٦) التكيف مع الغموض [0m

Perhaps the clearest exposition of the conundrum faced by firms in ambiguous environments, and their need to be both adapted and 
adaptable, is that by David Stark in his work on [3mheterarchies [0m: 

⋆ Stark, D. C. Recombinant property in East European capitalism. [3mAmerican Journal of Sociology, [0m101(4), 993–1027 (1996). 

⋆ Stark, D. C. Heterarchy: Distributing authority and organizing diversity. In Clippinger, J. H. (ed.), [3mThe Biology of Business: 
Decoding the Natural Laws of the Enterprise [0m(Jossey-Bass, San Francisco, 1999), chapter 7. 

⋆ Stark, D. C., and Bruszt, L. [3mPostsocialist Pathways: Transforming Politics and Property in East Central Europe [0m(Cambridge 
University Press, Cambridge, 1998). 

[1m(٧) الشبكات متعددة المستويات [0m

The properties of team-based, multiscale, and core-periphery networks are outlined in: 

• Dodds, P. S., Watts, D. J., and Sabel, C. F. The structure of optimal redistribution networks. Institute for Social and Economic 
Research and Policy Working Paper, Columbia University (2002). 

[1mالفصل العاشر: نهاية البداية [0m

The use of New York City (or more precisely, the borough of Manhattan) as an example of a complex system was inspired by John 
Holland’s opening chapter in: 

⋆ Holland, J. H. [3mHidden Order: How Adaptation Builds Complexity [0m(Perseus, Cambridge, MA, 1996). 

[1m(١) الحادي عشر من سبتمبر [0m

An excellent and detailed account of the September 11 attacks on the World Trade Center, and the monumental recovery effort that 
followed its collapse, is given in: 

⋆ Langewiesche, W. [3mAmerican Ground: Unbuilding the World Trade Center [0m(North Point Press, New York, 2002). 

The information about the police department’s communications predicament was derived from: 

⋆ Rashbaum, W. K. Police officers swiftly show inventiveness during crisis. [3mNew York Times, [0mSeptember 17, 2001, p. A7. 

The story about Cantor Fitzgerald was related by one of the survivors—the director of marketing and communications—who spoke at a 
roundtable discussion of business leaders at Columbia University on December 5, 2001. The roundtable was organized by David Stark 
and John Kelly, directors of Columbia’s Center for Organizational Innovation and Interactive Design Lab, respectively, and 
sponsored by Dr. Susan Gitelson. 

The article by Paul Krugman considering the economic consequences of the September 11 attacks in the context of an already 
faltering economy is: 

⋆ Krugman, P. Fear itself. [3mNew York Times Magazine, [0mSeptember 30, 2001, p. 36. 

[1m(٢) دروس لعصر متشابك [0m

An engaging and insightful account of the 1997 Asian crisis is contained in: 

⋆ Friedman, T. L. [3mThe Lexus and the Olive Tree: Understanding Globalization [0m(Farrar, Straus and Giroux, New York, 1999). 

Quite a lot of Harry Potter–related information can be found at http://www.insideharrypotter.com. 

And finally, a brief but illuminating account of the problems that beset Long Term Capital Management in the fall of 1998, is: 

⋆ MacKenzie, D. Fear in the markets. [3mLondon Review of Books, [0m22(8), 31–32 (2000).
